href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> In the late 1990s and early 2000s decade, Norway\'s <a href="/wiki/Dimmu_Borgir" title="Dimmu Borgir">Dimmu Borgir</a> brought black metal closer to the mainstream,<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> as did <a href="/wiki/Cradle_of_Filth" title="Cradle of Filth">Cradle of Filth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Power_metal">Power metal</span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Power_metal" title="Power metal">power metal</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hammerfall_group.jpg" class="image"><img alt="The band HammerFall is shown onstage after a concert. Three bass drums are in the drumkit." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Hammerfall_group.jpg/220px-Hammerfall_group.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Hammerfall_group.jpg/330px-Hammerfall_group.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Hammerfall_group.jpg/440px-Hammerfall_group.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1582" data-file-height="1066" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hammerfall_group.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Swedish power metal band <a href="/wiki/HammerFall" title="HammerFall">HammerFall</a> after a concert in <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>, Italy, in 2005.</div></div></div>\n<p>During the late 1980s, the power metal scene came together largely in reaction to the harshness of death and black metal.<sup id="cite_ref-Genre_-_Power_Metal_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Genre_-_Power_Metal-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> Though a relatively underground style in North America, it enjoys wide popularity in Europe, Japan, and South America. Power metal focuses on upbeat, epic melodies and themes that "appeal to the listener\'s sense of valor and loveliness".<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> The prototype for the sound was established in the mid-to-late 1980s by Germany\'s <a href="/wiki/Helloween" title="Helloween">Helloween</a>, which combined the power riffs, melodic approach, and high-pitched, "clean" singing style of bands like Judas Priest and Iron Maiden with thrash\'s speed and energy, "crystalliz[ing] the sonic ingredients of what is now known as power metal".<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Traditional power metal bands like Sweden\'s <a href="/wiki/HammerFall" title="HammerFall">HammerFall</a>, England\'s <a href="/wiki/DragonForce" title="DragonForce">DragonForce</a>, and America\'s <a href="/wiki/Iced_Earth" title="Iced Earth">Iced Earth</a> have a sound clearly indebted to the classic NWOBHM style.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> Many power metal bands such as America\'s <a href="/wiki/Kamelot" title="Kamelot">Kamelot</a>, Finnish groups <a href="/wiki/Nightwish" title="Nightwish">Nightwish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stratovarius" title="Stratovarius">Stratovarius</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sonata_Arctica" title="Sonata Arctica">Sonata Arctica</a>, Italy\'s <a href="/wiki/Rhapsody_of_Fire" title="Rhapsody of Fire">Rhapsody of Fire</a>, and Russia\'s <a href="/wiki/Catharsis_(Russian_band)" title="Catharsis (Russian band)">Catharsis</a> feature a keyboard-based <a href="/wiki/Symphonic_power_metal" class="mw-redirect" title="Symphonic power metal">"symphonic" sound</a>, sometimes employing orchestras and opera singers. Power metal has built a strong fanbase in Japan and South America, where bands like Brazil\'s <a href="/wiki/Angra_(band)" title="Angra (band)">Angra</a> and Argentina\'s <a href="/wiki/Rata_Blanca" title="Rata Blanca">Rata Blanca</a> are popular.<sup id="cite_ref-A-Z_of_Power_Metal_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A-Z_of_Power_Metal-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Closely related to power metal is <a href="/wiki/Progressive_metal" title="Progressive metal">progressive metal</a>, which adopts the complex compositional approach of bands like <a href="/wiki/Rush_(band)" title="Rush (band)">Rush</a> and <a href="/wiki/King_Crimson" title="King Crimson">King Crimson</a>. This style emerged in the United States in the early and mid-1980s, with innovators such as <a href="/wiki/Queensr%C3%BFche" title="Queensr\xc3\xbfche">Queensr\xc3\xbfche</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fates_Warning" title="Fates Warning">Fates Warning</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dream_Theater" title="Dream Theater">Dream Theater</a>. The mix of the progressive and power metal sounds is typified by New Jersey\'s <a href="/wiki/Symphony_X" title="Symphony X">Symphony X</a>, whose guitarist <a href="/wiki/Michael_Romeo" title="Michael Romeo">Michael Romeo</a> is among the most recognized of latter-day shredders.<sup id="cite_ref-Genre_-_Progressive_Metal_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Genre_-_Progressive_Metal-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;border:none; background:transparent; float:none; float:right">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width:1px"></td>\n<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em"><div class="haudio">\n<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:Helloween_halloween.ogg" title="File:Helloween halloween.ogg">"Halloween"</a></div>\n<div><div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_7" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="30.530793650794" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Helloween_halloween.ogg" data-mwprovider="local"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/bf/Helloween_halloween.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (144 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="143918" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/transcoded/b/bf/Helloween_halloween.ogg/Helloween_halloween.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="220472" /></audio></div></div>\n<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">Sample of <a href="/wiki/Helloween" title="Helloween">Helloween</a>\'s <i>Halloween</i> from <i><a href="/wiki/Keeper_of_the_Seven_Keys" title="Keeper of the Seven Keys">Keeper of the Seven Keys</a></i> (1987).</div></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Doom_metal">Doom metal</span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Doom_metal" title="Doom metal">doom metal</a></div>\n<p>Emerging in the mid-1980s with such bands as California\'s <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vitus_(band)" title="Saint Vitus (band)">Saint Vitus</a>, Maryland\'s <a href="/wiki/The_Obsessed" title="The Obsessed">The Obsessed</a>, Chicago\'s <a href="/wiki/Trouble_(band)" title="Trouble (band)">Trouble</a>, and Sweden\'s <a href="/wiki/Candlemass_(band)" title="Candlemass (band)">Candlemass</a>, the doom metal movement rejected other metal styles\' emphasis on speed, slowing its music to a crawl. Doom metal traces its roots to the lyrical themes and musical approach of early Black Sabbath.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Melvins" title="Melvins">Melvins</a> have also been a significant influence on doom metal and a number of its subgenres.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> Doom emphasizes melody, melancholy tempos, and a sepulchral mood relative to many other varieties of metal.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT1_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT1-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 1991 release of <i><a href="/wiki/Forest_of_Equilibrium" title="Forest of Equilibrium">Forest of Equilibrium</a></i>, the debut album by UK band <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_(band)" title="Cathedral (band)">Cathedral</a>, helped spark a new wave of doom metal. During the same period, the <a href="/wiki/Death/doom" class="mw-redirect" title="Death/doom">doom-death</a> fusion style of British bands <a href="/wiki/Paradise_Lost_(band)" title="Paradise Lost (band)">Paradise Lost</a>, <a href="/wiki/My_Dying_Bride" title="My Dying Bride">My Dying Bride</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Anathema_(band)" title="Anathema (band)">Anathema</a> gave rise to European gothic metal,<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> with its signature dual-vocalist arrangements, exemplified by Norway\'s <a href="/wiki/Theatre_of_Tragedy" title="Theatre of Tragedy">Theatre of Tragedy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tristania_(band)" title="Tristania (band)">Tristania</a>. New York\'s <a href="/wiki/Type_O_Negative" title="Type O Negative">Type O Negative</a> introduced an American take on the style.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;border:none; background:transparent; float:none; float:right">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width:1px"></td>\n<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em"><div class="haudio">\n<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:Burning_Witch_Country_Doctor.ogg" title="File:Burning Witch Country Doctor.ogg">"Country Doctor"</a></div>\n<div><div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_8" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="29.181519274376" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Burning_Witch_Country_Doctor.ogg" data-mwprovider="local"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/bc/Burning_Witch_Country_Doctor.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (99 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="99253" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/transcoded/b/bc/Burning_Witch_Country_Doctor.ogg/Burning_Witch_Country_Doctor.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="208240" /></audio></div></div>\n<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">"Country Doctor" from <i><a href="/wiki/Crippled_Lucifer" title="Crippled Lucifer">Crippled Lucifer</a></i> (1998) by doom metal band <a href="/wiki/Burning_Witch" title="Burning Witch">Burning Witch</a>.</div></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In the United States, <a href="/wiki/Sludge_metal" title="Sludge metal">sludge metal</a>, mixing doom and hardcore, emerged in the late 1980s\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/Eyehategod" title="Eyehategod">Eyehategod</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crowbar_(US_band)" class="mw-redirect" title="Crowbar (US band)">Crowbar</a> were leaders in a <a href="/wiki/Music_of_New_Orleans#Heavy_metal" title="Music of New Orleans">major Louisiana sludge scene</a>. Early in the next decade, California\'s <a href="/wiki/Kyuss" title="Kyuss">Kyuss</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sleep_(band)" title="Sleep (band)">Sleep</a>, inspired by the earlier doom metal bands, spearheaded the rise of <a href="/wiki/Stoner_metal" class="mw-redirect" title="Stoner metal">stoner metal</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> while Seattle\'s <a href="/wiki/Earth_(American_band)" title="Earth (American band)">Earth</a> helped develop the <a href="/wiki/Drone_metal" title="Drone metal">drone metal</a> subgenre.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> The late 1990s saw new bands form such as the Los Angeles\xe2\x80\x93based <a href="/wiki/Goatsnake" title="Goatsnake">Goatsnake</a>, with a classic stoner/doom sound, and <a href="/wiki/Sunn_O)))" title="Sunn O)))">Sunn O)))</a>, which crosses lines between doom, drone, and <a href="/wiki/Dark_ambient" title="Dark ambient">dark ambient</a> metal\xe2\x80\x94the <i>New York Times</i> has compared their sound to an "<a href="/wiki/Music_of_India" title="Music of India">Indian</a> <a href="/wiki/Raga" title="Raga">raga</a> in the middle of an earthquake".<sup id="cite_ref-NYT1_246-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT1-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s_and_early_2000s_subgenres_and_fusions">1990s and early 2000s subgenres and fusions</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Alternative_metal" title="Alternative metal">alternative metal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rap_metal" title="Rap metal">rap metal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nu_metal" title="Nu metal">nu metal</a>, <a href="/wiki/NWOAHM" class="mw-redirect" title="NWOAHM">NWOAHM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Industrial_metal" title="Industrial metal">industrial metal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Groove_metal" title="Groove metal">groove metal</a></div>\n<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;border:none; background:transparent; float:none; float:right">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width:1px"></td>\n<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em"><div class="haudio">\n<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:Panterawalk.ogg" title="File:Panterawalk.ogg">"Walk" by Pantera (1992)</a></div>\n<div><div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_9" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="30.031746031746" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Panterawalk.ogg" data-mwprovider="local"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/8c/Panterawalk.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (113 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="113098" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/transcoded/8/8c/Panterawalk.ogg/Panterawalk.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="113448" /></audio></div></div>\n<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">"<a href="/wiki/Walk_(Pantera_song)" title="Walk (Pantera song)">Walk</a>" from <a href="/wiki/Pantera" title="Pantera">Pantera</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Display_of_Power" title="Vulgar Display of Power">Vulgar Display of Power</a></i> (1992), exemplifying the groove metal style.</div></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The era of heavy metal\'s mainstream dominance in North America came to an end in the early 1990s with the emergence of <a href="/wiki/Nirvana_(band)" title="Nirvana (band)">Nirvana</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Grunge" title="Grunge">grunge</a> bands, signaling the popular breakthrough of <a href="/wiki/Alternative_rock" title="Alternative rock">alternative rock</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> Grunge acts were influenced by the heavy metal sound, but rejected the excesses of the more popular metal bands, such as their "flashy and virtuosic solos" and "appearance-driven" <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> orientation.<sup id="cite_ref-Covach_200-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Covach-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Glam metal fell out of favor due not only to the success of grunge,<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> but also because of the growing popularity of the more aggressive sound typified by Metallica and the post-thrash <a href="/wiki/Groove_metal" title="Groove metal">groove metal</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pantera" title="Pantera">Pantera</a> and <a href="/wiki/White_Zombie_(band)" title="White Zombie (band)">White Zombie</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> In 1991, the band <a href="/wiki/Metallica" title="Metallica">Metallica</a> released their album <i><a href="/wiki/Metallica_(album)" title="Metallica (album)">Metallica</a></i>, also known as <i>The Black Album</i>, which moved the band\'s sound out of the <a href="/wiki/Thrash_metal" title="Thrash metal">thrash metal</a> genre and into standard heavy metal.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup> The album was certified 16\xc3\x97 Platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">RIAA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> A few new, unambiguously metal bands had commercial success during the first half of the decade\xe2\x80\x94Pantera\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Far_Beyond_Driven" title="Far Beyond Driven">Far Beyond Driven</a></i> topped the <i>Billboard</i> chart in 1994\xe2\x80\x94but, "In the dull eyes of the mainstream, metal was dead".<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> Some bands tried to adapt to the new musical landscape. Metallica revamped its image: the band members cut their hair and, in 1996, headlined the alternative musical festival <a href="/wiki/Lollapalooza" title="Lollapalooza">Lollapalooza</a> founded by <a href="/wiki/Jane%27s_Addiction" title="Jane&#39;s Addiction">Jane\'s Addiction</a> singer <a href="/wiki/Perry_Farrell" title="Perry Farrell">Perry Farrell</a>. While this prompted a backlash among some long-time fans,<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> Metallica remained one of the most successful bands in the world into the new century.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Staley05.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A male singer, Layne Staley, performs onstage with Alice in Chains. He holds the microphone with both hands and his eyes are closed as he sings." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Staley05.jpg/220px-Staley05.jpg" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Staley05.jpg/330px-Staley05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Staley05.jpg/440px-Staley05.jpg 2x" data-file-width="863" data-file-height="587" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Staley05.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Layne_Staley" title="Layne Staley">Layne Staley</a> of <a href="/wiki/Alice_in_Chains" title="Alice in Chains">Alice in Chains</a>, one of the most popular acts identified with <a href="/wiki/Alternative_metal" title="Alternative metal">alternative metal</a> performing in 1992.</div></div></div>\n<p>Like Jane\'s Addiction, many of the most popular early 1990s groups with roots in heavy metal fall under the umbrella term "alternative metal".<sup id="cite_ref-alternativemetal_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alternativemetal-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> Bands in Seattle\'s grunge scene such as <a href="/wiki/Soundgarden" title="Soundgarden">Soundgarden</a>, credited as making a "place for heavy metal in alternative rock",<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Alice_in_Chains" title="Alice in Chains">Alice in Chains</a> were at the center of the alternative metal movement. The label was applied to a wide spectrum of other acts that fused metal with different styles: <a href="/wiki/Faith_No_More" title="Faith No More">Faith No More</a> combined their alternative rock sound with punk, <a href="/wiki/Funk" title="Funk">funk</a>, metal, and <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a>; <a href="/wiki/Primus_(band)" title="Primus (band)">Primus</a> joined elements of funk, punk, <a href="/wiki/Thrash_metal" title="Thrash metal">thrash metal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Experimental_music" title="Experimental music">experimental music</a>; <a href="/wiki/Tool_(band)" title="Tool (band)">Tool</a> mixed metal and <a href="/wiki/Progressive_rock" title="Progressive rock">progressive rock</a>; bands such as <a href="/wiki/Fear_Factory" title="Fear Factory">Fear Factory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ministry_(band)" title="Ministry (band)">Ministry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nine_Inch_Nails" title="Nine Inch Nails">Nine Inch Nails</a> began incorporating metal into their <a href="/wiki/Industrial_music" title="Industrial music">industrial sound</a>, and vice versa, respectively; and <a href="/wiki/Marilyn_Manson_(band)" title="Marilyn Manson (band)">Marilyn Manson</a> went down a similar route, while also employing shock effects of the sort popularized by Alice Cooper. Alternative metal artists, though they did not represent a cohesive scene, were united by their willingness to experiment with the metal genre and their rejection of glam metal aesthetics (with the stagecraft of Marilyn Manson and White Zombie\xe2\x80\x94also identified with alt-metal\xe2\x80\x94significant, if partial, exceptions).<sup id="cite_ref-alternativemetal_259-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alternativemetal-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> Alternative metal\'s mix of styles and sounds represented "the colorful results of metal opening up to face the outside world."<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the mid- and late 1990s came a new wave of U.S. metal groups inspired by the alternative metal bands and their mix of genres.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> Dubbed "nu metal", bands such as <a href="/wiki/Slipknot_(band)" title="Slipknot (band)">Slipknot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Linkin_Park" title="Linkin Park">Linkin Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Limp_Bizkit" title="Limp Bizkit">Limp Bizkit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Papa_Roach" title="Papa Roach">Papa Roach</a>, <a href="/wiki/P.O.D." title="P.O.D.">P.O.D.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Korn" title="Korn">Korn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Disturbed_(band)" title="Disturbed (band)">Disturbed</a> incorporated elements ranging from <a href="/wiki/Death_metal" title="Death metal">death metal</a> to hip hop, often including <a href="/wiki/DJ" class="mw-redirect" title="DJ">DJs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rapping" title="Rapping">rap</a>-style vocals. The mix demonstrated that "pancultural metal could pay off".<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> Nu metal gained mainstream success through heavy MTV rotation and Ozzy Osbourne\'s 1996 introduction of <a href="/wiki/Ozzfest" title="Ozzfest">Ozzfest</a>, which led the media to talk of a resurgence of heavy metal.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> In 1999, <i>Billboard</i> noted that there were more than 500 specialty metal radio shows in the United States, nearly three times as many as ten years before.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> While nu metal was widely popular, traditional metal fans did not fully embrace the style.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> By early 2003, the movement\'s popularity was on the wane, though several nu metal acts such as Korn or Limp Bizkit retained substantial followings.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Recent_styles:_mid.E2.80.93late_2000s_and_2010s"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_styles:_mid\xe2\x80\x93late_2000s_and_2010s">Recent styles: mid\xe2\x80\x93late 2000s and 2010s</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"New metal" redirects here. For the genre of music with a similar name, see <a href="/wiki/Nu_metal" title="Nu metal">nu metal</a>.</div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Metalcore" title="Metalcore">metalcore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Djent" title="Djent">djent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deathcore" title="Deathcore">deathcore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melodic_metalcore" title="Melodic metalcore">melodic metalcore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mathcore" title="Mathcore">mathcore</a>, and <a href="/wiki/NWOAHM" class="mw-redirect" title="NWOAHM">NWOAHM</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Metalcore" title="Metalcore">Metalcore</a>, a hybrid of extreme metal and <a href="/wiki/Hardcore_punk" title="Hardcore punk">hardcore punk</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> emerged as a commercial force in the mid-2000s decade. Through the 1980s and 1990s, metalcore was mostly an underground phenomenon;<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> pioneering bands include <a href="/wiki/Earth_Crisis" title="Earth Crisis">Earth Crisis</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-am_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-am-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ig_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ig-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> other prominent bands include <a href="/wiki/Converge_(band)" title="Converge (band)">Converge</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-am_270-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-am-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hatebreed" title="Hatebreed">Hatebreed</a><sup id="cite_ref-ig_271-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ig-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rh_272-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rh-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Shai_Hulud_(band)" class="mw-redirect" title="Shai Hulud (band)">Shai Hulud</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-killyour_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-killyour-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> By 2004, melodic metalcore\xe2\x80\x94influenced as well by <a href="/wiki/Melodic_death_metal" title="Melodic death metal">melodic death metal</a>\xe2\x80\x94was popular enough that <a href="/wiki/Killswitch_Engage" title="Killswitch Engage">Killswitch Engage</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_End_of_Heartache" title="The End of Heartache">The End of Heartache</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Shadows_Fall" title="Shadows Fall">Shadows Fall</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_War_Within_(Shadows_Fall_album)" title="The War Within (Shadows Fall album)">The War Within</a></i> debuted at numbers 21 and 20, respectively, on the <i>Billboard</i> album chart.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Masters_of_Rock_2007_-_Children_of_Bodom_-_08.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A color photograph of two members of the group Children of Bodom standing on a stage with guitars, drums are visible in the background. Both electric guitarists have &quot;flying V&quot; style guitars and they have long hair." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Masters_of_Rock_2007_-_Children_of_Bodom_-_08.jpg/200px-Masters_of_Rock_2007_-_Children_of_Bodom_-_08.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Masters_of_Rock_2007_-_Children_of_Bodom_-_08.jpg/300px-Masters_of_Rock_2007_-_Children_of_Bodom_-_08.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Masters_of_Rock_2007_-_Children_of_Bodom_-_08.jpg/400px-Masters_of_Rock_2007_-_Children_of_Bodom_-_08.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Masters_of_Rock_2007_-_Children_of_Bodom_-_08.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Children_of_Bodom" title="Children of Bodom">Children of Bodom</a>, performing at the 2007 <a href="/wiki/Masters_of_Rock_(festival)" title="Masters of Rock (festival)">Masters of Rock</a> festival.</div></div></div>\n<p>Evolving even further from metalcore comes <a href="/wiki/Mathcore" title="Mathcore">mathcore</a>, a more rhythmically complicated and progressive style brought to light by bands such as <a href="/wiki/The_Dillinger_Escape_Plan" title="The Dillinger Escape Plan">The Dillinger Escape Plan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Converge_(band)" title="Converge (band)">Converge</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Protest_the_Hero" title="Protest the Hero">Protest the Hero</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> Mathcore\'s main defining quality is the use of odd time signatures, and has been described to possess rhythmic comparability to <a href="/wiki/Free_jazz" title="Free jazz">free jazz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Heavy metal remained popular in the 2000s, particularly in continental Europe. By the new millennium Scandinavia had emerged as one of the areas producing innovative and successful bands, while Belgium, The Netherlands and especially Germany were the most significant markets.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> Metal music is more favorably embraced in Scandinavia and Northern Europe than other regions due to social and political openness in these regions.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup> Established continental metal bands that placed multiple albums in the top 20 of the German charts between 2003 and 2008, including Finnish band <a href="/wiki/Children_of_Bodom" title="Children of Bodom">Children of Bodom</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup> Norwegian act Dimmu Borgir,<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup> Germany\'s <a href="/wiki/Blind_Guardian" title="Blind Guardian">Blind Guardian</a><sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup> and Sweden\'s HammerFall.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 2000s, an extreme metal fusion genre known as <a href="/wiki/Deathcore" title="Deathcore">deathcore</a> emerged. Deathcore incorporates elements of <a href="/wiki/Death_metal" title="Death metal">death metal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hardcore_punk" title="Hardcore punk">hardcore punk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Metalcore" title="Metalcore">metalcore</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> Deathcore features characteristics such as death metal <a href="/wiki/Riff" class="mw-redirect" title="Riff">riffs</a>, hardcore punk <a href="/wiki/Breakdown_(music)" title="Breakdown (music)">breakdowns</a>, death growling, "pig squeal"-sounding vocals, and screaming.<sup id="cite_ref-Cosmo_Lee_286-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cosmo_Lee-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup> Deathcore bands include <a href="/wiki/Whitechapel_(band)" title="Whitechapel (band)">Whitechapel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suicide_Silence" title="Suicide Silence">Suicide Silence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Despised_Icon" title="Despised Icon">Despised Icon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carnifex_(band)" title="Carnifex (band)">Carnifex</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dawn_of_the_Deathcore_288-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dawn_of_the_Deathcore-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>\nThe term "retro-metal" has been used to describe bands such as Texas-based <a href="/wiki/The_Sword" title="The Sword">The Sword</a>, California\'s <a href="/wiki/High_on_Fire" title="High on Fire">High on Fire</a>, Sweden\'s <a href="/wiki/Witchcraft_(band)" title="Witchcraft (band)">Witchcraft</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-AMAgeofWinters_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMAgeofWinters-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup> and Australia\'s <a href="/wiki/Wolfmother" title="Wolfmother">Wolfmother</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AMAgeofWinters_289-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMAgeofWinters-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WRS_290-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WRS-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup> The Sword\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Age_of_Winters" title="Age of Winters">Age of Winters</a></i> (2006) drew heavily on the work of Black Sabbath and <a href="/wiki/Pentagram_(band)" title="Pentagram (band)">Pentagram</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Begrand2006_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Begrand2006-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup> Witchcraft added elements of <a href="/wiki/Folk_rock" title="Folk rock">folk rock</a> and psychedelic rock,<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> and Wolfmother\'s <a href="/wiki/Wolfmother_(album)" title="Wolfmother (album)">self-titled 2005 debut album</a> had "<a href="/wiki/Deep_Purple" title="Deep Purple">Deep Purple</a>-ish organs" and "<a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Page" title="Jimmy Page">Jimmy Page</a>-worthy chordal <a href="/wiki/Ostinato" title="Ostinato">riffing</a>". <a href="/wiki/Mastodon_(band)" title="Mastodon (band)">Mastodon</a>, which plays in a progressive/sludge style, has inspired claims of a metal revival in the United States, dubbed by some critics the "<a href="/wiki/New_Wave_of_American_Heavy_Metal" class="mw-redirect" title="New Wave of American Heavy Metal">New Wave of American Heavy Metal</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup></p><div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<p>By the early 2010s, metalcore was evolving to more frequently incorporate synthesizers and elements from genres beyond rock and metal. The album <i><a href="/wiki/Reckless_%26_Relentless" title="Reckless &amp; Relentless">Reckless &amp; Relentless</a></i> by British band <a href="/wiki/Asking_Alexandria" title="Asking Alexandria">Asking Alexandria</a> (which sold 31,000 copies in its first week), and The Devil Wears Prada\'s 2011 album <i><a href="/wiki/Dead_Throne" title="Dead Throne">Dead Throne</a></i> (which sold 32,400 in its first week)<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup> reached up to number 9 and 10,<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup> respectively, on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 chart. In 2013, British band <a href="/wiki/Bring_Me_the_Horizon" title="Bring Me the Horizon">Bring Me the Horizon</a> released their fourth studio album <a href="/wiki/Sempiternal_(album)" title="Sempiternal (album)">Sempiternal</a> to critical acclaim. The album debuted at number 3 on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Album_Chart" class="mw-redirect" title="UK Album Chart">UK Album Chart</a> and at number 1 in Australia. The album sold 27,522 copies in the US, and charted at number 11 on the US Billboard Chart, making it their highest charting release in America until their follow-up album <i><a href="/wiki/That%27s_the_Spirit" title="That&#39;s the Spirit">That\'s the Spirit</a></i> debuted at no. 2 in 2015.\n</p><p>Also in the 2010s, a metal style called "<a href="/wiki/Djent" title="Djent">djent</a>" developed as a spinoff of standard <a href="/wiki/Progressive_metal" title="Progressive metal">progressive metal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-secrets_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-secrets-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup> Djent music uses rhythmic and technical complexity,<sup id="cite_ref-Concealingfate_298-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Concealingfate-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup> heavily distorted, <a href="/wiki/Palm_mute" title="Palm mute">palm-muted</a> guitar chords, syncopated <a href="/wiki/Riffs" class="mw-redirect" title="Riffs">riffs</a><sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_299-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-299">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Polyrhythm" title="Polyrhythm">polyrhythms</a> alongside <a href="/wiki/Virtuoso" title="Virtuoso">virtuoso</a> soloing.<sup id="cite_ref-secrets_296-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-secrets-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup> Another typical characteristic is the use of extended range <a href="/wiki/Seven-string_guitar" title="Seven-string guitar">seven</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eight-string_guitar" title="Eight-string guitar">eight</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nine-string_guitar" title="Nine-string guitar">nine-string guitars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> Djent bands include <a href="/wiki/Periphery_(band)" title="Periphery (band)">Periphery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tesseract_(band)" title="Tesseract (band)">Tesseract</a><sup id="cite_ref-Concealingfate_298-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Concealingfate-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Textures_(band)" title="Textures (band)">Textures</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sharon_Osbourne_(8082324151).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Sharon_Osbourne_%288082324151%29.jpg/140px-Sharon_Osbourne_%288082324151%29.jpg" width="140" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Sharon_Osbourne_%288082324151%29.jpg/210px-Sharon_Osbourne_%288082324151%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Sharon_Osbourne_%288082324151%29.jpg/280px-Sharon_Osbourne_%288082324151%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sharon_Osbourne_(8082324151).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sharon Osbourne would become the manager for several bands, but is most remembered for her work with Ozzy Osbourne and Mot\xc3\xb6rhead.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:20160210_Bochum_Halestorm_Halestorm_0265.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/20160210_Bochum_Halestorm_Halestorm_0265.jpg/220px-20160210_Bochum_Halestorm_Halestorm_0265.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/20160210_Bochum_Halestorm_Halestorm_0265.jpg/330px-20160210_Bochum_Halestorm_Halestorm_0265.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/20160210_Bochum_Halestorm_Halestorm_0265.jpg/440px-20160210_Bochum_Halestorm_Halestorm_0265.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4245" data-file-height="2825" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:20160210_Bochum_Halestorm_Halestorm_0265.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lzzy Hale of Halestorm.</div></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Women_in_heavy_metal">Women in heavy metal</span></h2>\n<p>The history of women in heavy metal can be traced back as far as the 1970s when the band <a href="/wiki/Vixen_(band)" title="Vixen (band)">Vixen</a> was formed in 1973. Another hard rock band that featured all-female members, <a href="/wiki/The_Runaways" title="The Runaways">The Runaways</a>, would be founded in 1975. And while The Runaways may have been lost to time, two former members would rise to fame in solo careers. Those being <a href="/wiki/Joan_Jett" title="Joan Jett">Joan Jett</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lita_Ford" title="Lita Ford">Lita Ford</a>, who would have successful rock careers.<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup> In 1978, with the rise of the <a href="/wiki/New_wave_of_British_heavy_metal" title="New wave of British heavy metal">new wave of British heavy metal</a>, the band <a href="/wiki/Girlschool" title="Girlschool">Girlschool</a> would be founded, who are best known for their collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Mot%C3%B6rhead" title="Mot\xc3\xb6rhead">Mot\xc3\xb6rhead</a> in 1980 under the pseudonym <a href="/wiki/Headgirl" title="Headgirl">Headgirl</a>. In 1996, Finnish band <a href="/wiki/Nightwish" title="Nightwish">Nightwish</a> was founded and has featured women as vocalists. This would lead to a surplus of heavy metal bands featuring women as lead singers, such as Grammy Award winners <a href="/wiki/Halestorm" title="Halestorm">Halestorm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delain" title="Delain">Delain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Within_Temptation" title="Within Temptation">Within Temptation</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Epica_(band)" title="Epica (band)">Epica</a> among others.<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Women have had an important role behind the scenes, such as <a href="/wiki/Gaby_Hoffmann_(manager)" title="Gaby Hoffmann (manager)">Gaby Hoffmann</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sharon_Osbourne" title="Sharon Osbourne">Sharon Osbourne</a>. In 1981, Hoffmann would help <a href="/wiki/Don_Dokken" title="Don Dokken">Don Dokken</a> acquire his first record deal.<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup> Hoffmann also became the manager of <a href="/wiki/Accept_(band)" title="Accept (band)">Accept</a> in 1981 and wrote songs under the pseudonym of "Deaffy" for many of band\'s studio albums. In the band\'s newer albums, vocalist <a href="/wiki/Mark_Tornillo" title="Mark Tornillo">Mark Tornillo</a> stated that Hoffmann still had some influence in songwriting.<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup> Osbourne, the wife and manager of <a href="/wiki/Ozzy_Osbourne" title="Ozzy Osbourne">Ozzy Osbourne</a>, would found the <i><a href="/wiki/Ozzfest" title="Ozzfest">Ozzfest</a></i> music festival and manage several bands, included Mot\xc3\xb6rhead, <a href="/wiki/Coal_Chamber" title="Coal Chamber">Coal Chamber</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Smashing_Pumpkins" title="The Smashing Pumpkins">The Smashing Pumpkins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_Light_Orchestra" title="Electric Light Orchestra">Electric Light Orchestra</a>, Lita Ford and <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" Vice<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">7 January</span> 2017</span>. <q>In almost every subgenre of heavy metal, synthesizers held sway. Look at Cynic, who on their progressive death metal opus Focus (1993) had keyboards appear on the album and during live performances, or British gothic doom band My Dying Bride, who relied heavily on synths for their 1993 album, Turn Loose the Swans. American noise band Today is the Day used synthesizers on their 1996 self titled album to powerfully add to their din. Voivod even put synthesizers to use for the first time on 1991\'s Angel Rat and 1993\'s The Outer Limits, played by both guitarist Piggy and drummer Away. The 1990s were a gold era for the use of synthesizers in heavy metal, and only paved the way for the further explorations of the new millennia.</q></cite><span Revolver magazine<span class="reference-accessdate">.
